SECTION 1
PROJECT CONSIDERATIONS
The project involves installation of an outbound PM contraflow lane and widening of the
outbound side of the Pearl City Viaduct on Interstate Route H 1 on the Island of Oahu Hawaii
The project location and general vicinity are shown on the Project Location Map Plate 1 The
project includes the following items
1
Installation of an outbound zipper lane using moveable concrete barrier MCB
system that is compatible with the existing inbound zipper lane This outbound
lane would be deployed using the existing equipment and would provide an
outbound contraflow lane for afternoon traffic to the leeward areas This
additional lane would extend for a distance of about 6 1 miles from the vicinity
of Radford Drive to the Waiawa Interchange
2
Rehabilitation of the existing eastbound lanes of the highway between Waiau
Interchange and Kaimakani Street including reconstruction of pavements lifting
of existing PCC pavements and installation of new traffic safety elements such
as signage markings and guard rails
3
Improvements to the Pearl City and Waimalu Viaducts including full depth deck
repairs and restoration of signage markings and traffic control
A summary of the field exploration program conducted for the Interstate Route H 1
Contraflow Lane Phase 2 project is presented below Detailed information and discussions for
each specific work item are provided in the respective appendices of this geotechnical data
report

SECTION 2
SCOPE OF WORK
The purpose of our field exploration and laboratory testing program is to obtain an
overview of the surface and subsurface conditions along the project site to support the design
of the widening of the Pearl City Viaduct structure In order to accomplish this we conducted a
field exploration and laboratory testing program consisting of the following tasks and efforts
1
Preparation of an accident prevention plan for our work on the highway and
roads
2
Filing of application for permits to drill and utility clearances
3
Preparation of traffic control plans and provision of police officers and safety
devices for traffic control and or lane closures at selected boring locations
during our field exploration program
4
Mobilization and demobilization of truck and track mounted drill rigs water
trucks and operators to and from the project site
5
Drilling and sampling of twenty four 24 borings extending to depths ranging
from about 37 5 to 109 5 feet below the existing ground pavement surface for a
total of about 2 068 lineal feet of exploration
6
Coordination of the field exploration and logging of the borings by our
geologists engineers
7
Performance of ten 10 seismic piezocone penetration tests SCPTu at ten
selected locations extending to depths of about 20 5 to 84 0 feet below the
existing ground surface
8
Performance of seismic shear wave velocity profiling using seismic cone
penetration test SCPT equipment at fourteen 14 selected investigation
locations to depths of about 84 0 to 102 3 feet for seismic design considerations
9
Laboratory testing of selected soil and core samples retrieved from our field
exploration as an aid in classifying the materials and evaluating their engineering
properties
10
Preparation of this geotechnical data report presenting the results of the
geotechnical data review subsurface explorations and laboratory tests
11
Coordination of our overall work on the project by our senior engineer
SECTION 2 SCOPE OF WORK

12
Quality assurance of our work on the project by our principal engineer
13
Miscellaneous work efforts such as drafting word processing and clerical
support

SECTION 3
SITE CHARACTERIZATION
3 1
Regional Geology
The Island of Oahu was built by the extrusion of basaltic lava from the Waianae and
Koolau shield volcanoes The older Waianae Volcano is estimated to be middle to late Pliocene
in age and the Koolau Volcano is estimated to be late Pliocene to early Pleistocene in age As
the volcanic activity at Waianae Volcano ceased lava flows from Koolau Volcano banked
against its eroded eastern slope forming the Schofield Plateau
The Koolau Volcanic Shield was built during the late Pliocene and early Pleistocene by
the extrusion of successive thin bedded lava flows The main shield building stage ceased
approximately 2 5 million years ago Evidence from historic drilled wells indicates that the
Island of Oahu has subsided as much as 1 200 feet since the cessation of the early volcanic
activity Macdonald and Abbott 1970 During the period of island subsidence coral algal reefs
began to grow along the southern coast of Oahu forming embayments protected by the barrier
reefs A series of lagoons formed behind the barrier reefs and both terrigenous and marine
sediments accumulated in the lagoons Macdonald and Abbott 1970
During the Pleistocene Epoch Ice Age many sea level changes occurred as a result of
widespread glaciation in the continental areas of the world As the great continental glaciers
accumulated the level of the oceans fell because there was less water available to fill the
oceanic basins Conversely as the glaciers receded melted global sea levels rose because the
volume of water increased
The land mass comprising the Island of Oahu remained essentially stable during these
sea level changes and the fluctuations were eustatic in nature These glacio eustatic
fluctuations resulted in stands of the sea that were both higher transgression and lower
regression relative to present sea level on the Island of Oahu Sedimentation and stream
erosion occurring during the sea level fluctuations complicated the geologic history and
evolution of the Island of Oahu especially along the coastal regions of the island where the
effects of sea level change are most prominent
SECTION 3 SITE CHARACTERIZATION
W O 6400 00
GEOLABS INC
Page 7
Hawaii California
The higher sea level stands caused some substantial landform changes including the
accumulation of deltas and alluvial fans composed of terrigenous sediments in the heads of the
old bays The accumulation of reef deposits at corresponding higher elevations and the
accumulation of lagoonal and or marine sediments in the quiet lagoonal waters protected by
the barrier reefs The concurrent growth of reefs and the accumulation of lagoonal sediments
also resulted in the deposition of coral algal limestone and coral reef ledge materials embedded
within the predominantly lagoonal sedimentary unit
The lower sea level stands caused terrestrial streams to incise drainages into the
evolving coastal plain platforms composed of sedimentary and coral reef deposits In addition
subaerial exposure of the calcareous sediments caused consolidation of the soft deltaic
materials and lagoonal deposits and the induration of calcareous reef materials Furthermore
renewed subaerial erosion acting at the upper elevations of the volcanic shield caused the
downstream transport and deposition of terrigenous alluvial sediments under relatively higher
energy conditions
During periods of no significant sea level change continued meandering stream action
extended the alluvial deltas and fans seaward and deposited terrestrial alluvial materials
overlying the older marine lagoonal sediments
The project site is within the lowland coastal alluvial plains along the southern distal
flank of the Koolau Mountain Range The coastal plain surfaces are relatively flat to gently
undulating in the easterly to westerly direction Two primary waterways traverses the project
site with the eastern waterway discharging into East Loch and the western waterway
discharging into Middle Loch of Pearl Harbor The meandering streams have contributed
significantly to the erosional evolution and deposition of the coastal alluvial plains by incising
into the underlying basaltic rock Koolau Basalt comprising the basement rock formation of this
portion of the Island of Oahu
On the Pearl City Aiea coastal plains and vicinity the sedimentary wedge of alluvial
materials is referred to as caprock overlying the basal aquifer The capping material keeps the
basal aquifer under a confining water pressure therefore artesian flow conditions may be
SECTION 3 SITE CHARACTERIZATION
W O 6400 00
GEOLABS INC
Page 8
Hawaii California
encountered when the basal aquifer with sufficient groundwater head is pierced and a conduit
is provided extending toward the ground surface
In summary the project site is located on the Southern Oahu Coastal Plain near the
shoreline of East and Middle Loch of Pearl Harbor and traverses Waimano and Waiawa
Streams In general the subsurface materials underlain by the project site consist of alluvial
soils underlain by basalt rock formation The alluvial deposits are overlain by recent fills
3 2
Subsurface Characteristics
In general we observed four main stratigraphic units within the project site The
stratigraphic units consist of soil and rock materials of varying character and engineering
properties The four main stratigraphic units are listed below in the general order of geologic
age beginning with the youngest unit and ending with the oldest unit
1
Recent Fill Rf
2
Recent Alluvium Ra
3
Older Alluvium Qa
4
Tertiary Koolau Basalt Tkb
The following sections briefly describe the general characteristics of each of the above
stratigraphic units based on our literature research past experience with similar materials and
the field exploration and laboratory testing program conducted at selected locations along the
project site The approximate delineation of these stratigraphic units at the ground surface
along the project site is presented on the Geology Map Plate 3
Recent Fill Rf
This stratigraphic unit represents low lying areas that were filled during urbanization
The majority of these low lying areas is underlain at relatively shallow depths by recent
alluvium and was originally marsh areas In higher elevation areas the surface fills are
underlain by older alluvial soil deposits The fill materials generally consist of clayey silts
and silty clays with soft to very stiff consistencies and clayey silty sands and gravels
with some cobbles and boulders
SECTION 3 SITE CHARACTERIZATION
W O 6400 00
GEOLABS INC
Page 9
Hawaii California
The quality and composition of the fill materials are variable These fills were frequently
placed without proper compaction control Therefore it is difficult to make any general
statement regarding their engineering properties or construction in these areas
Recent Alluvium Ra
These soils generally are the result of sedimentation in a very low energy environment
such as an estuary or bay Frequently the soils assigned to this unit accumulated very
rapidly under water and might not have been exposed to air Therefore there is a
tendency to encounter under consolidated OCR Over Consolidation Ratio 1 0
sediments which settle under the weight of minimal overburden or structural loading
Recent alluvium generally is found within some stream channels and bordering some
stream banks at the mouths outlets of streams and within broad valley floors and
basin features surrounded by hills These soils also may be found in proximity to swamp
and tidal flat environments The following subunits are used in this geotechnical data
report
Recent Alluvium
This subunit generally consists of brown to gray silty clays and clayey silts with
varying amounts of sands and infrequent pockets of gravel and cobbles The
consistency is generally in the range of soft to medium stiff In addition this
subunit consists of very loose to loose silty sands and gravels
Marsh Estuarine Deposit
This subunit generally consists of dark gray silts and clays with fibrous organic
materials in a very soft to soft consistency This soil unit contains traces of fine to
medium grained sands They are characterized by a moderate to strong organic
odor and may contain small fragile mollusk shells
Older Alluvium Qa
Older alluvial deposits are generally stiff to hard silty and clayey soils that originally were
deposited in alluvial environments buried over long periods of time by more recent
deposits to become consolidated and then subsequently uncovered at the ground
SECTION 3 SITE CHARACTERIZATION
W O 6400 00
GEOLABS INC
Page 10
Hawaii California
surface by erosion or other geologic processes This unit generally overlies the Koolau
Basalt and consists of terrigenous sediments which have been transported by stream
action from the upper reaches of the streams
Gravel lenses representing buried stream channel sometimes are encountered Portions
of the Older Alluvium unit contain some weathered basaltic cobbles and boulders These
coarse grained parts of the unit also may contain artesian groundwater from the basal
fresh water system or as a sub aquifer The deposits may resemble saprolite soil
deposits but they are clearly differentiable by the layered characteristics These
materials frequently show a moderate to high shrink swell potential when subjected to
fluctuations in moisture The following subunits are used in this geotechnical data
report
These soils generally consist of brown to gray clays and silts with varying amounts of
sands and infrequent pockets of gravel and cobbles The consistency is generally in the
range of stiff to hard In addition these soils consist of medium dense to very dense
silty sands and gravels and cobbles and boulders
Tertiary Koolau Basalt Tkb
Koolau Basalt is the oldest geologic unit within the project site Generally it consists of
a a and pahoehoe flows of basaltic lavas and may have a mantle of cobbles and
boulders or residual soils overlying the top of the basalt formation In addition it is
anticipated that various types of volcanic rock sub components such as clinker layers
and lava tubes also may be encountered within the basalt formation The following
subunits of the Koolau Basalt are used in this geotechnical data report
Residual Soil
This subunit consists of soils produced from the in situ chemical weathering of
the basic rock originating from Koolau Basalt These soils generally consist of
hard grayish brown clayey silts The soils are usually structureless and may
have a blocky texture
SECTION 3 SITE CHARACTERIZATION
W O 6400 00
GEOLABS INC
Page 11
Hawaii California
Saprolite
Saprolite essentially is derived from the tropical weathering of volcanic
formations which may contain intrusive rock bodies of variable composition
such as basalt andesite etc Saprolite is a form of residual soil that exhibits a
relict structure from the parent rock Structural features such as vesicles and
joints are visible in saprolite This subunit consists of predominantly silty sand
and gravel soils containing variations in color with varying degrees of mottling
Clinker
Clinker is the fragmental basalt found on the top and sometimes at the bottom
of a a lava flows Clinker generally is gravel to cobble sized fragments of
scoriaceous rock in a tightly packed but open graded structure
Basalt Formation
This subunit is used to designate the in situ lava formation This subunit occurs
as gray or brown severely fractured to massive soft to very hard rock formation
Groundwater
Groundwater level measurements were taken during advancement of the boreholes
drilled
for
the
project
during
our
field
exploration
program
We
encountered groundwater level in the borings drilled at depths ranging from about 2 to
33 5 feet below the existing ground and or pavement surface The groundwater levels
measured generally correspond to about Elevations 4 1 to 48 5 feet Mean Sea Level
MSL The water level measurements collected are shown on the Logs of Borings It
should be noted that some of the measurements collected may not reflect the static
groundwater level as the water level within the drilled boring could still be affected by
the wash boring drilling technique used and consisted likely of drill water Experience
has shown that groundwater levels also are seasonally dependent

SECTION 4
GEOTECHNICAL EXPLORATION PROGRAM
The geotechnical exploration program conducted for Interstate Route H 1 Contraflow
Phase 2 project generally consisted of the following field and laboratory work components
A brief description of each work component is presented below Detailed discussions findings
and test results of the various components are provided in the respective appendices herein
In addition subsurface information along the project site also is available from As Built
1967 and January 1968 The boring logs are presented in Appendix F
4 1
Soil Borings Rock Coring and Associated Field Testing
Soil and rock sampling methods and field testing are described in more detail in the
introduction to Appendix A The following discussion provides an overview of the methods and
procedures
Typically soil borings were advanced with 4 inch diameter continuous flight solid stem
augers SSA to the first encounter with groundwater and then continued with PQ size wireline
coring methods to advance the PQ size casing from the ground surface In general auger
drilling was used in areas where stiff to hard cohesive soils older alluvium exist and in
locations where rock coring is not anticipated Additionally SSA drilling was switched over to
the wireline coring method when hard clays boulders and or rock formation were
encountered or when soft and or loose soils that caved in were encountered
Sampling of the soils was performed at 5 foot intervals Drive samples were obtained
using the Modified California sampler ASTM D3550 and the Standard Penetration Test SPT
split spoon sampler ASTM D1586 In the softer soils relatively undisturbed samples were
obtained by driving a ring lined Modified California sampler ASTM D3550 and undisturbed
samples were obtained for testing by pushing a 3 inch OD thin walled steel Shelby tube
ASTM D1587 into the soil formation
SECTION 4 GEOTECHNICAL EXPLORATION PROGRAM
W O 6400 00
GEOLABS INC
Page 13
Hawaii California
Where the borehole was advanced utilizing the PQ core barrel in the soil formations
samples of the soils recovered from the PQ core barrel also were retained in core boxes for
visual observation Intervals where the borehole was advanced utilizing the PQ casing only as a
rotary wash drilling method there were no soil samples collected The borings were advanced
into the rock formations with the PQ size wireline coring methods The PQ size wireline coring
methods produce rock core samples that are 3 35 inches 85 mm in diameter
In situ testing of the subsurface materials in the borings included the SPT which was
performed in accordance with sampling provides a measure of the resistance
or consistency of a soil and is reported as the uncorrected N value which is defined as the
number of blows required to drive a standard split spoon sampler 12 inches with a 140 pound
hammer after 6 inches of initial seating The penetration resistance of the Modified California
sampler was recorded in a similar manner and the Modified California sampler blows per
12 inches can be approximately related to the SPT N value through correlation
Rock core recovery REC and rock quality designation RQD were measured as
described in Appendix A ASTM D6032 Standard Test Method for Determining Rock Quality
Designation RQD of Rock Core states that Core sizes from BQ to PQ with core diameters of
1 44 in to 35 in respectively are normally acceptable for measuring RQD
as long as proper drilling techniques are used that do not cause excessive core breakage or
the optimal core sizes for measuring RQD The RQD is also useful for large core diameters
provided the core diameter is clearly stated The rock core photographs are included in
Appendix E for information and reference
During the field exploration program our geologists engineers performed pocket
penetrometer tests on selected cohesive soil samples Pocket penetrometer tests provide an
indication of the unconfined compressive strength of a soil sample The pocket penetrometer
test values are shown on the Logs of Borings in Appendix A and summarized on Tables D 1 1
through D 1 23 in Appendix D In addition torvane shear tests were performed on selected
SECTION 4 GEOTECHNICAL EXPLORATION PROGRAM
W O 6400 00
GEOLABS INC
Page 14
Hawaii California
cohesive soil samples to get an indication of the shear strength of a soil sample The torvane
shear test values are shown on the Logs of Borings in Appendix A
4 2
Seismic Piezocone Penetration Testing
Seismic piezocone penetration testing SCPTu was performed at ten selected locations
using seismic piezocone equipment also referred to as Seismic CPT SCPTu The test
procedures are discussed in more detail in Appendix B In brief a steel cone connected to a
friction sleeve is hydraulically pushed into the soil and the tip resistance sleeve friction and
piezometric pore pressures are measured providing information that can be correlated to the
soil type and behavior in a virtually continuous profile with depth SCPTu testing can be
performed only to the depths to which the cone tip can be hydraulically pushed with our
truck mounted drill rig set up Ten 10 seismic piezocone penetration tests were performed at
ten selected locations Boring 249 and 250 for
the project
The seismic cone tip contains a geophone sensor At a succession of depths the
advancement of the cone tip was halted a seismic pulse was generated at the ground surface
by striking a loaded plank with a switched hammer and the resulting seismic shear wave was
detected at the geophone The distance from the source and the wave arrival time allow for
determination of the average shear wave velocity over a depth interval The seismic piezocone
penetration test records are presented in Appendix B
4 3
Seismic Shear Wave Velocity Testing
Seismic shear wave velocity profiling was performed at fourteen of the completed
boreholes Boring 253 256 and
258 using seismic cone penetration testing SCPT equipment Procedures are discussed in
more detail in Appendix C In brief the completed borehole was tremie filled with time release
bentonite pellets and bentonite chips in order to provide a medium through which the seismic
cone tip could be pushed The sleeve and tip resistance through the bentonite filled borehole
are not meaningful because the cone is pushed through the bentonite backfill however the
seismic wave travels from the ground surface through the surrounding soils allowing
SECTION 4 GEOTECHNICAL EXPLORATION PROGRAM
W O 6400 00
GEOLABS INC
Page 15
Hawaii California
measurement of the average seismic shear wave velocity in the same manner as described
above for the SCPTu
The seismic cone tip contains a geophone sensor At a succession of depths the
advancement of the cone tip was halted a seismic pulse was generated at the ground surface
by striking a loaded plank with a switched hammer and the resulting seismic shear wave was
detected at the geophone The distance from the source and the wave arrival time allow for
determination of the average shear wave velocity over a depth interval The measured average
seismic shear wave velocity logs are presented in Appendix C
4 4
Laboratory Testing
Laboratory testing was performed on soil and rock samples to determine the physical
and engineering properties Laboratory tests performed included moisture content unit
weight Atterberg limits grain size distribution consolidation direct shear unconsolidated
undrained UU triaxial compression uniaxial compressive strength of rock California Bearing
Ratio and modified proctor The laboratory test results are provided in Appendix D

SECTION 5
LIMITATIONS
The geotechnical field and laboratory test data submitted in this geotechnical data
report are based upon information obtained from the field exploration points The locations
and elevations of the field exploration points indicated in this report were estimated from
as built drawings dated 1967 and 1968 for the Pearl City Viaduct project
The stratification lines shown on the graphic representations of the field exploration
points depict the approximate boundaries between soil and rock types and as such may
denote a gradual transition Water level data presented on the logs of borings in this report
were based on measurements recorded in the borings at the times shown on the graphic
representations It should be noted that fluctuation of the water level may occur due to
variation in tides rainfall temperature and other factors
This report has been prepared for the exclusive use of Wilson Okamoto Corporation and
their client State of Hawaii Department of Transportation for specific application to the
Interstate Route H 1 PM Contraflow Lane Phase 2 project in accordance with generally
accepted geotechnical engineering principles and practices Therefore this report has been
prepared solely for the purpose of assisting the engineers in the preparation of the design and
construction documents for the project
This geotechnical data report was not intended to investigate the potential for
presence of hazardous materials existing at the project site It should be noted that the
equipment techniques and personnel used to conduct a geo environmental exploration differ
substantially from those applied in geotechnical engineering
END OF LIMITATIONS

A P P E N D I X A
Test Boring Exploration
We explored the subsurface conditions at the Interstate Route H 1 PM Contraflow
Phase 2 project by drilling and sampling 24 borings designated as Boring Nos B 200 B 204
depths ranging from about 37 5 to 109 5 feet below the existing ground pavement surface
using various truck and track mounted drill rigs equipped with continuous flight augers and
rotary coring tools The field exploration was conducted from through
The boring locations are summarized in Table 2 and are shown on the
Site Plans Plates 2 1 through 2 8
Soil borings were advanced with 4 inch diameter continuous flight solid stem augers
SSA to the first encounter with groundwater and then continued with PQ size wireline coring
methods to advance the PQ size casing from the ground surface In general auger drilling was
used in areas where stiff to hard cohesive soils older alluvium exist and in locations where
rock coring was not anticipated Additionally SSA drilling was switched over to wireline coring
method when hard clays boulders and or rock formation were encountered or when soft
and or loose soils that caved in were encountered
Our geologists engineers classified the materials encountered in the borings by visual
and textural examination in the field in general accordance with ASTM D2488 Standard
Practice for Description and Identification of Soils and monitored the drilling operations on a
near continuous basis These classifications were further reviewed visually and by testing in the
laboratory Soils were classified in general accordance with ASTM D2487 Standard Practice for
Classification of Soils for Engineering Purposes Unified Soil Classification System as shown on
the Soil Log Legend Plate A 0 1 Graphic representations of the materials encountered and
other observations such as groundwater levels etc are presented on the Logs of Borings
Relatively undisturbed soil samples were obtained from the borings drilled in general
accordance with ASTM D3550 Standard Practice for Thick Wall Ring Lined Spilt Barrel Drive
Sampling of Soils by driving a 3 inch OD modified California sampler with a 140 pound hammer
falling 30 inches In addition some samples were obtained from the borings drilled in general
accordance with ASTM D1586 Standard Test Method for Penetration Test and Split Barrel
Sampling of Soils by driving a 2 inch OD standard penetration sampler using the same hammer
and drop The blow counts needed to drive the sampler the second and third 6 inches of an
18 inch drive are shown as the Penetration Resistance on the Logs of Borings at the
appropriate sample depths Undisturbed samples of the soft soil formation were obtained by
pushing a 3 inch OD thin walled stainless steel Shelby tube into the soil formation in general
accordance with ASTM D 1587 Standard Practice for Thin Walled Tube Sampling of Soils for
Geotechnical Purposes The range of hydraulic pressures needed to advance the sampler
Appendix A
Test Boring Exploration
W O 6400 00
GEOLABS INC
AUGUST 2015 Page A 2
Hawaii California
through a 24 inch push is shown as the Penetration Resistance on the Logs of Borings at the
appropriate sample depths
Pocket penetrometer tests were performed on selected cohesive soil samples retrieved
in the field The pocket penetrometer test provides an indication of the unconfined
compressive strength of the soil sample Results of the pocket penetrometer tests are
appropriate sample depths
Core samples of the rock materials encountered at the project site were obtained by
using diamond core drilling techniques consisting of a PQ wireline coring system with double
tube core barrel core size of 3 35 inches in general accordance with ASTM D2113 Diamond
Core Drilling for Site Investigation Core drilling is a rotary drilling method that uses a hollow bit
to cut into the rock formation The rock material left in the hollow core of the bit is
mechanically recovered for examination and description The coring rates indicated on the Logs
of Borings refer to the time required to complete that particular core run at that depth Rock
cores were described in general accordance with the Rock Description System as shown on the
Rock Log Legend Plate A 0 2 The Rock Description System is based generally on the publication
Suggested Methods for the Quantitative Description of Discontinuities in Rock Masses by
International Society for Rock Mechanics March 1977
Recovery REC is defined as the actual length of material recovered from a coring
attempt versus the length of the core attempt For example if 3 7 feet of material is recovered
from a 5 0 foot core run the recovery would be 74 percent and would be shown on the Logs of
Borings as REC 74
The Rock Quality Designation RQD is also a subjective guide to the relative quality of
rock masses RQD is defined as the percentage of the total core run in rock that is sound
material in excess of 4 inches in length without any discontinuities discounting any drilling
mechanical and handling induced fractures or breaks If 2 5 feet of sound material is recovered
from a 5 0 foot core run in rock the RQD would be 50 percent and would be shown on the Logs
of Borings as RQD 50 Generally the following is used to describe the relative quality of the
rock based on the Practical Handbook of Physical Properties of Rocks and Minerals by
Robert S Carmichael 1989

APPENDIX B
W O 6400 00
GEOLABS INC
AUGUST 2015 Page B 1
Hawaii California
A P P E N D I X B
Seismic Piezocone Penetration Tests
Geolabs Inc conducted cone penetration testing using the seismic piezocone
B 207 SCPT
B 208 SCPT
B 209 SCPT
B 216A SCPT
B 216B SCPT
B 239 SCPT
The tests were performed in general accordance with ASTM D5778 Standard Test
Method for Performing Electronic Friction Cone and Piezocone Penetration Testing of Soils The
probes extended to depths of about 20 5 to 84 0 feet below the existing ground surface using
seismic piezocone penetration testing equipment SCPTU before refusal conditions to our
system were encountered
The seismic piezocone penetration test consists of hydraulically pushing a 10 ton steel
electronic subtraction cone Serial Number DSG1063 manufactured by Vertek with an apex
angle of 60 degrees and an area of 1 55 square inches 10 square centimeters connected to a
friction sleeve with an area of 23 25 square inches 150 square centimeters into the ground at
A catalog cut of the 10 ton electronic subtraction cone and the manufacturer calibration report
illustration information purposes only
The tip and side friction resistance and pore pressure induced immediately behind the
cone tip designated as the U2 parameter during penetration are measured by strain gauges
within the instrument and are recorded versus the depth of penetration at about 2 inch
5 millimeter intervals When the material encountered was too hard for further penetration
by the SCPTU equipment which might cause potential equipment damage penetration was
halted and the cone was withdrawn
The cone carries a uniaxial horizontal geophone with an embedded inclinometer to
detect the arrival of a shear wave propagated from the ground surface The seismic
measurements are made when the SCPTU has stopped and a shear wave is sent into the
subsurface A shear wave is generated at the surface by striking a loaded plank in opposite
directions with a switched hammer at approximately 6 foot intervals The propagation time of
the wave from the hammer blow to the cone was measured at each depth interval The vector
difference of these depths divided by the time difference provided the average shear wave
velocity over the depth interval
The field data collected was subsequently processed in the office using the computer
software program CPT Coneplot developed by Vertek Logs of the seismic piezocone
cone tip resistance friction ratio sleeve friction over tip resistance pore pressure local
Appendix B
Seismic Piezocone Penetration Test
W O 6400 00
GEOLABS INC
AUGUST 2015 Page B 2
Hawaii California
friction seismic shear wave velocity soil behavior based on the Rf zone and interpreted soil
description Values of the tip resistance friction ratio and pore pressure may be correlated to
soil strength and classification The center of the friction sleeve is approximately 4 inches
100 mm behind the cone tip To calculate the friction ratio the average friction resistance and
tip resistance are compared at the same depth This involves an offset of the friction resistance
by the physical distance of 4 inches The soil behavior is determined using the average tip
resistance and the friction ratio over approximately 14 inches 350 mm using Robertson s 1986
soil classification chart as shown on Figure B 3
Pore pressure is presented in terms of equivalent height of water head fresh water
The equilibrium water pressure was estimated based on depth below water surface at the test
location and the density of fresh water

Cones Data Acquisition Systems
10 15 Ton Digital Cones for E4FCS
Temperature Compensated The digital electronic subtraction 10 and 15
ton cones have been developed to address the accuracy sensitivity and dura
bility problems inherent in other cone designs with a resolution of 6 5 and 10
Ibs respectively The unit consists of a single element strain gauge transducer
eliminating mechanical coupling effects and with cone support electron
ics packaged directly behind the transducer Both the cone tip local friction
element and pore pressure element are ﬁ eld replaceable by the operator in
approximately ﬁ ve minutes The cones are conﬁ gured with one through ﬁ ve
channel capacity with six channels from which to choose

There are two possible locations for pore pressure on the tip or directly be
hind the tip
The electronics have precision power supplies for the strain gauges which
eliminate the effects of cable resistance on the measurements Subtraction is
performed digitally by the CPU and calibration data for tip local friction and
pore pressure channels is stored in CPU non volatile memory Digital cone
calibration is capable of correcting for non linearity and hysterisis in a way
that analog circuitry cannot Digital cones conform to all international stan
dards

APPENDIX C

A P P E N D I X C
Seismic Shear Wave Velocity Tests
Seismic shear wave velocity profiling of the subsurface materials was performed using
Seismic Cone Penetration Testing SCPT equipment Seismic shear wave velocity testing using
seismic cone penetration test equipment was performed at fourteen selected investigation
The seismic shear wave velocity profiling was performed at approximately 6 foot
intervals extending to depths of about 84 0 to 102 3 feet below the existing ground pavement
surface In order to conduct the shear wave velocity test in the boring the test boring generally
was advanced utilizing rotary coring methods to the maximum depth of the boring Logs of the
materials encountered in the boring are presented on the Logs of Borings in Appendix A After
the boring was advanced to the maximum depth of the borehole the bored hole was backfilled
with 0 25 inch diameter time release bentonite pellets The temporary casing from the coring
operations was used as a tremie pipe to place the bentonite pellets starting from the bottom
and advancing upward When the bentonite pellets are in contact with the groundwater in the
borehole the pellets started to hydrate slowly As the bentonite pellets hydrate they swell and
soften Backfilling above the static groundwater table were performed in stages by adding
water to limited amount of bentonie chips to ensure hydration before additional bentonite
chips were placed in the borehole The probe was then pushed through the softened bentonite
extending to depths of about 84 0 to 102 3 feet below the existing ground pavement surface
using the seismic cone penetration testing equipment SCPT
The seismic shear wave velocity test consists of hydraulically pushing a 10 ton steel
electronic subtraction cone into the bentonite backfilled borehole The cone has an apex angle
of 60 degrees and a projected surface area of 1 55 square inches 10 square centimeters
equipped with an electronic depth sensor attached to the cone rod The seismic cone carries a
uniaxial horizontal geophone to detect the arrival of a shear wave generated and propagated
from the ground surface Seismic measurements are made when the SCPT has stopped and a
shear wave is sent into the subsurface A shear wave is generated at the surface by striking a
loaded plank with a switched hammer The propagation time of the wave from the hammer
blow to the cone was measured at each discrete depth interval The vector difference of these
depths divided by the time difference for the shear wave to arrive at the various depths
provided the average shear wave velocity over the depth interval
The shear wave velocities measured and the average shear wave velocity calculated for
the top 100 feet unless noted otherwise of the soil profile at the boring locations are
Appendix C
Seismic Shear Wave Velocity Tests

APPENDIX D
W O 6400 00
GEOLABS INC
AUGUST 2015 Page D 1
Hawaii California
A P P E N D I X D
Laboratory Tests
Samples recovered from our field exploration program performed for the Interstate
Route H 1 PM Contraflow Phase 2 project were visually examined and classified in our
laboratory in Honolulu Hawaii Selected samples were tested to evaluate the physical
characteristics and engineering properties of the soils encountered The laboratory testing
program was formulated with the emphasis on evaluating the moisture density plasticity
gradation compressibility and shear strength of the soils encountered
The laboratory tests performed included determination of dry density and natural
moisture content Atterberg Limits sieve analysis consolidation direct shear triaxial
compression unconfined compression California Bearing Ratio and modified proctor tests
through 2 3 and are presented on Plates D 1 through D 69 Detailed descriptions of the various
tests performed for this exploration are presented below
Moisture and Density
Moisture Content and Dry Density tests were performed on selected soil samples to aid
in defining the interface between the various soil layers encountered and correlating the layers
between test borings The moisture content tests were performed in general accordance with
presented on the Logs of Borings at the appropriate sample depths
Atterberg Limits
Thirty eight 38 Atterberg Limits tests were performed on selected soil samples to
evaluate the liquid limit LL plastic limit PL and plasticity index PI as an aid in classifying
the soils The Atterberg Limits tests were performed in general accordance with ASTM D 4318
The test results are summarized on the Logs of Borings at the appropriate sample depths and in
through D 4
Sieve Analysis
To provide information on the particle size distribution of the soils encountered
fourteen 14 Sieve Analysis tests were performed to evaluate the gradation characteristics and
to aid in soil classification The tests were performed in accordance with ASTM C117 and C136
Graphic presentation of the test results are provided on Plates D 5 through D 7 The test results
Appendix D
Laboratory Tests
W O 6400 00
GEOLABS INC
AUGUST 2015 Page D 2
Hawaii California
Consolidation
Four 4 Consolidation tests were performed on selected soil samples to evaluate the
compressibility characteristics of the on site soils The tests were performed in accordance with
ASTM D2435 and the test results are plotted on Plates D 8 through D 11
Direct Shear
To evaluate the shear strength characteristics of the in situ soils three 3 strain
controlled consolidated drained Direct Shear tests were performed on the in situ soil samples
in accordance with ASTM D3080 The test results are presented on Plates D 12 through D 14
Unconsolidated Undrained Triaxial Compression
To evaluate the undrained shear strength of the soils fifty two 52 Unconsolidated
Undrained Triaxial Compression TXUU tests were performed on selected in situ soil samples in
accordance with ASTM D2850 The approximate in situ effective overburden pressure was used
as the applied confining pressure for the undisturbed samples The test results and the
stress strain curves are presented on Plates D 15 through D 66
Uniaxial Compressive Strength Rock Cores
Fourteen 14 Uniaxial Compressive Strength tests ASTM D7012 Method C were
performed on selected rock cores to evaluate their unconfined compressive strength of the
rock formation encountered Uniaxial compressive strength test results for the selected rock
cores are presented on Plate D 67
California Bearing Ratio
One laboratory California Bearing Ratio CBR test ASTM D1883 was performed on a bulk
sample of the near surface soils to evaluate the pavement support characteristics of the soils The
sample was remolded to near the optimum moisture content of the soils Compaction of the
sample was performed by dropping a 10 pound hammer from a height of 18 inches The sample
was compacted in five equal layers with each layer receiving 56 blows of energy The sample was
soaked in water prior to the penetration test The test results are presented on Plate D 68
Modified Proctor
One Modified Proctor compaction test ASTM D1557 was performed on a bulk sample of
the near surface soils to evaluate the dry density and moisture content relationships The test
results are presented on Plate D 69
